        <tr>
         <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
          <div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
           <ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em;"> 
            <li value="1"><a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossetian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> languages are official languages<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></li> 
           </ol>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><b>South Ossetia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">j</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <small>less commonly</small> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of South Ossetia – the State of Alania</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> or the <b>Tskhinvali Region</b>, is a <i>de facto</i> state in the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a> <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">recognised by most countries</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>. It has an officially stated population of just over 53,000 people, who live in an area of 3,900&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>, south of the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasian_Federal_District" title="North Caucasian Federal District">Russian Caucasus</a>, with 30,000 living in <a href="/wiki/Tskhinvali" title="Tskhinvali">Tskhinvali</a>. The separatist polity, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_South_Ossetia" title="Government of South Ossetia">Republic of South Ossetia</a> (or the <i>State of Alania</i>), is <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">recognized as a state</a> by <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> While Georgia lacks control over South Ossetia, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Government of Georgia (country)">Georgian government</a> and most members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> consider the territory part of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, whose constitution designates the area as "the former autonomous district of South Ossetia", in reference to the <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_Autonomous_Oblast" title="South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast">South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast</a> disbanded in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Georgia does not recognize the existence of South Ossetia as a political entity, and therefore its territory does not correspond to any Georgian administrative area (although <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Administration_of_South_Ossetia" title="Provisional Administration of South Ossetia">Provisional Administration of South Ossetia</a> was created by the Georgian authorities as a transitional measure leading to the settlement of South Ossetia's status), with most of the territory included into <a href="/wiki/Shida_Kartli" title="Shida Kartli">Shida Kartli</a> region. The area is often informally referred to as the legally undefined <i>Tskhinvali Region</i><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[nb 1]</a></sup> in both Georgia and international organisations when neutrality is deemed necessary. </p>
      <p>The South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast, created in 1922, <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_independence" title="Declaration of independence">declared independence</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> in 1991. The <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgian</a> government responded by abolishing South Ossetia's autonomy and trying to re-establish its control over the region by force.<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> The crisis escalation led to the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_South_Ossetia_War" class="mw-redirect" title="1991–92 South Ossetia War">1991–92 South Ossetia War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Georgians fighting against those controlling South Ossetia occurred on two other occasions, in 2004 and 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-king_fivedaywar_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-king_fivedaywar-16">[15]</a></sup> The latter conflict led to the <a href="/wiki/Russo%E2%80%93Georgian_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo–Georgian War">Russo–Georgian War</a>, during which Ossetian and Russian forces gained full <i>de facto</i> control of the territory of the former South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast. In the wake of the 2008 war, Georgia and a significant part of the international community consider South Ossetia to be <a href="/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia" title="Occupied territories of Georgia">occupied by the Russian military</a>. </p>
      <p>South Ossetia relies heavily on military, political and financial aid from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_Army_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy_Army-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_and_early_modern_period">Medieval and early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Medieval and early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The territory of contemporary South Ossetia was part of the ancient Georgian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Iberia" title="Kingdom of Iberia">Kingdom of Iberia</a>, the latter was <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia#Unification_of_the_Georgian_State" title="Kingdom of Georgia">unified</a> under the single <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Georgian monarchy</a> in 11th-century, extending its possessions up to <a href="/wiki/Dvaleti" title="Dvaleti">Dvaleti</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a> are believed to originate from the <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, an nomadic <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranian</a> tribe.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> In the 8th century a consolidated Alan kingdom, referred to in sources of the period as <a href="/wiki/Alania" title="Alania">Alania</a>, emerged in the northern Caucasus Mountains. Around 1239–1277 Alania fell to the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol</a> and later to the <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a>'s armies, that massacred much of the Alanian population. The survivors among the Alans retreated into the mountains of the central Caucasus and gradually started migration to the south. </p>
      <p>In 1299, <a href="/wiki/Gori,_Georgia" title="Gori, Georgia">Gori</a> was captured by the <a href="/wiki/Alania" title="Alania">Alan</a> tribesmen fleeing the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">Mongol conquest</a> of their original homeland in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>. The Georgian king <a href="/wiki/George_V_of_Georgia" title="George V of Georgia">George V</a> recovered the town in 1320, pushing the Alans back over the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasus mountains">Caucasus mountains</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 17th century, by pressure of <a href="/wiki/Kabardians" title="Kabardians">Kabardian</a> princes, Ossetians started a second wave of migration from the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a> to Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> Ossetian peasants, who were migrating to the mountainous areas of the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a>, often settled in the lands of Georgian feudal lords.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199438_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199438-21">[20]</a></sup> The Georgian King of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli" title="Kingdom of Kartli">Kingdom of Kartli</a> permitted Ossetians to immigrate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199439_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199439-22">[21]</a></sup> According to Russian ambassador to Georgia <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikhail_Tatishchev&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mikhail Tatishchev (page does not exist)">Mikhail Tatishchev</a>, at the beginning of the 17th century there was already a small group of Ossetians living near the headwaters of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Liakhvi_River" title="Greater Liakhvi River">Greater Liakhvi River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199439_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199439-22">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> In the 1770s there were more Ossetians living in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli_(1484%E2%80%931762)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Kartli (1484–1762)">Kartli</a> than ever before. This period has been documented in the travel diaries of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Anton_G%C3%BCldenst%C3%A4dt" title="Johann Anton Güldenstädt">Johann Anton Güldenstädt</a> who visited Georgia in 1772. The Baltic German explorer called modern <a href="/wiki/North_Ossetia" class="mw-redirect" title="North Ossetia">North Ossetia</a> simply Ossetia, while he wrote that Kartli (the areas of modern-day South Ossetia) was populated by Georgians and the mountainous areas were populated by both Georgians and Ossetians.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199440_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199440-24">[23]</a></sup> Güldenstädt also wrote that the northernmost border of Kartli is the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">Major Caucasus Ridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199437_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199437-25">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> By the end of 18th century, the ultimate sites of Ossetian settlement on the territory of modern South Ossetia were in Kudaro (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Jejora&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jejora (page does not exist)">Jejora</a> river estuary), <a href="/wiki/Greater_Liakhvi_River" title="Greater Liakhvi River">Greater Liakhvi</a> gorge, the gorge of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Little_Liakhvi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Little Liakhvi (page does not exist)">Little Liakhvi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ksani" title="Ksani">Ksani</a> River gorge, Guda (<a href="/wiki/Aragvi_River" title="Aragvi River">Tetri Aragvi</a> estuary) and Truso (<a href="/wiki/Terek_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Terek River">Terek</a> estuary).<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_review_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_review-28">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Georgian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli-Kakheti" title="Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti">Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti</a>, part of which was the major territory of modern South Ossetia, was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> in 1801. Ossetian migration to Georgian areas continued in the 19th and 20th centuries, when <a href="/wiki/Georgia_within_the_Russian_Empire" title="Georgia within the Russian Empire">Georgia was part of the Russian Empire</a> and Ossetian settlements in <a href="/wiki/Trialeti" title="Trialeti">Trialeti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borjomi_Municipality" title="Borjomi Municipality">Borjomi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bakuriani" title="Bakuriani">Bakuriani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kakheti" title="Kakheti">Kakheti</a> emerged as well.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_review_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_review-28">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Ossetia_as_a_part_of_the_Soviet_Union">South Ossetia as a part of the Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: South Ossetia as a part of the Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">Russian revolution</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouleimanov201399_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouleimanov201399-29">[28]</a></sup> the area of modern South Ossetia became part of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Democratic Republic of Georgia">Democratic Republic of Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013112–113_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013112–113-30">[29]</a></sup> In 1918, <a href="/wiki/Georgian%E2%80%93Ossetian_conflict_(1918%E2%80%9320)" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian–Ossetian conflict (1918–20)">conflict began</a> between the landless Ossetian peasants living in <a href="/wiki/Shida_Kartli" title="Shida Kartli">Shida Kartli</a> (Interior Georgia), who were influenced by <a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" title="Bolshevism">Bolshevism</a> and demanded ownership of the lands they worked, and the <a href="/wiki/Mensheviks" title="Mensheviks">Menshevik government</a> backed ethnic Georgian aristocrats, who were legal owners. Although the Ossetians were initially discontented with the economic policies of the central government, the tension soon transformed into ethnic conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013112–113_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013112–113-30">[29]</a></sup> The first Ossetian rebellion began in February 1918, when three Georgian princes were killed and their land was seized by the Ossetians. The central government of <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tiflis</a> retaliated by sending the National Guard to the area. However, the Georgian unit retreated after they had engaged the Ossetians.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> Ossetian rebels then proceeded to occupy the town of <a href="/wiki/Tskhinvali" title="Tskhinvali">Tskhinvali</a> and began attacking the ethnic Georgian civilian population. During uprisings in 1919 and 1920, the Ossetians were covertly supported by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Soviet Russia</a>, but even so, were defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013112–113_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013112–113-30">[29]</a></sup> According to allegations made by Ossetian sources, the crushing of the 1920 uprising caused the death of 5,000 Ossetians, while ensuing hunger and epidemics were the causes of death of more than 13,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png/250px-Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png/375px-Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png/500px-Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png 2x" data-file-width="1461" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Georgian_soviet_republic1957_1991.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> in 1957–1991
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Soviet Georgian government, established after the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_invasion_of_Georgia" title="Red Army invasion of Georgia">Red Army invasion of Georgia</a> in 1921, created an autonomous administrative unit for <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasian</a> Ossetians in April 1922 under pressure from <a href="/wiki/Kavbiuro" title="Kavbiuro">Kavbiuro</a> (the Caucasian Bureau of the Central Committee of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Russian Communist Party</a>), called the <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_Autonomous_Oblast" title="South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast">South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast (AO)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question1994153–161_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question1994153–161-32">[31]</a></sup> Some believe that the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a> granted this autonomy to the Ossetians in exchange for their help in fighting the Democratic Republic of Georgia and favoring local separatists, since this area had never been a <a href="/wiki/Territorial_entity" title="Territorial entity">separate entity</a> prior to the Russian invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-roudik_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roudik-33">[32]</a></sup> The drawing of administrative boundaries of the South Ossetian AO was quite a complicated process. Many Georgian villages were included within the South Ossetian AO despite numerous protests by the Georgian population. While the city of <a href="/wiki/Tskhinvali" title="Tskhinvali">Tskhinvali</a> did not have a majority Ossetian population, it was made the capital of the South Ossetian AO.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question1994153–161_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question1994153–161-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> In addition to parts of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gori_Uyezd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gori Uyezd (page does not exist)">Gori Uyezd</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dusheti_Uyezd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dusheti Uyezd (page does not exist)">Dusheti Uyezd</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tiflis_Governorate" title="Tiflis Governorate">Tiflis Governorate</a>, parts of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Racha_Uyezd&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Racha Uyezd (page does not exist)">Racha Uyezd</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kutaisi_Governorate" class="mw-redirect" title="Kutaisi Governorate">Kutaisi Governorate</a> (western Georgia) were also included within the South Ossetian AO. All these territories historically had been indigenous Georgian lands.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199472–73_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199472–73-35">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Historical Ossetia in the North Caucasus did not have its own political entity before 1924, when the <a href="/wiki/North_Ossetian_Autonomous_Oblast" title="North Ossetian Autonomous Oblast">North Ossetian Autonomous Oblast</a> was created.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199472–73_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199472–73-35">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although the Ossetians had their own language (<a href="/wiki/Ossetic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ossetic language">Ossetian</a>), Russian and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a> were administrative/state languages.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-36">[35]</a></sup> Under the rule of Georgia's government during Soviet times, Ossetians enjoyed minority cultural autonomy, including speaking the Ossetian language and teaching it in schools.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-36">[35]</a></sup> In 1989, two-thirds of Ossetians in the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic">Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> lived outside the South Ossetian AO.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199442_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOssetian_Question199442-37">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Georgian-Ossetian_conflict">Georgian-Ossetian conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Georgian-Ossetian conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Georgian-Ossetian_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian-Ossetian conflict">Georgian-Ossetian conflict</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span id="1989.E2.80.932008"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1989–2008">1989–2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1989–2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Tensions in the region began to rise amid rising nationalism among both Georgians and Ossetians in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> Before this, the two communities of the <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_Autonomous_Oblast" title="South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast">South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast</a> of the Georgian SSR had been living in peace with each other except for the <a href="/wiki/Georgian-Ossetian_conflict_(1918-1920)" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian-Ossetian conflict (1918-1920)">1918–1920 events</a>. Both ethnicities have had a high level of interaction and high rates of intermarriage.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Dispute surrounding the presence of the Ossetian people in the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a> has been one of the causes of conflict. Although Georgian historiography believes that Ossetian mass migration to the South Caucasus (Georgia) began in the 17th century, Ossetians claim to have been residing in the area since ancient times and that present-day South Ossetia is their historical homeland.<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> No evidence exists to back up the Ossetian claims of being <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> to South Ossetia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013119_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouleimanov2013119-39">[38]</a></sup> Some Ossetian historians accept that the migration of Ossetian ancestors to modern South Ossetia began after the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Georgia_and_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol invasions of Georgia and Armenia">Mongol invasions</a> of the 13th century, while one South Ossetian <i>de facto</i> foreign minister in the 1990s admitted that the Ossetians first appeared in the area only in the early 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-40">[39]</a></sup> Since it was created after the Russian invasion of 1921, South Ossetia was regarded as artificial creation by Georgians during the Soviet era.<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The South Ossetian Popular Front (<i>Ademon Nykhas</i>) was created in 1988. On 10 November 1989, the South Ossetian regional council asked the Georgian Supreme Council to upgrade the region to the status of an "<a href="/wiki/Autonomous_republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous republics of the Soviet Union">autonomous republic</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> The decision to transform the South Ossetian AO into the South Ossetian <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republics of the Soviet Union">ASSR</a> by the South Ossetian authorities escalated the conflict. On 11 November, this decision was revoked by the Georgian parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> The Georgian authorities removed the First Party Secretary of the oblast from his position.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Georgian Supreme Council adopted a law barring regional parties in summer 1990. Since this was interpreted by South Ossetians as a move against Ademon Nykhas, they declared full sovereignty as part of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Soviet_Socialist_Republics" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Soviet Socialist Republics">Union of Soviet Socialist Republics</a> (USSR) on 20 September 1990. Ossetians boycotted subsequent Georgian parliamentary elections and held their own contest in December.<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 1990, the parliamentary election in Georgia was won by <a href="/wiki/Zviad_Gamsakhurdia" title="Zviad Gamsakhurdia">Zviad Gamsakhurdia</a>'s "Round Table" block.<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> On 11 December 1990, Zviad Gamsakhurdia's government declared the Ossetian election illegitimate and abolished South Ossetia's autonomous status altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-icg_14-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icg-14">[13]</a></sup> Gamsakhurdia rationalized the abolition of Ossetian autonomy by saying, "They [Ossetians] have no right to a state here in Georgia. They are a national minority. Their homeland is North Ossetia.... Here they are newcomers."<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-40">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When the Georgian parliament declared a state of emergency in the territory of South Ossetian AO on 12 December 1990, troops from both Georgian and Soviet interior ministries were sent to the region. After the Georgian National Guard was formed in early 1991, Georgian troops entered Tskhinvali on 5 January 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-dk_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dk-44">[43]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_South_Ossetia_War" class="mw-redirect" title="1991–92 South Ossetia War">1991–92 South Ossetia War</a> was characterised by general disregard for international humanitarian law by uncontrollable militias, with both sides reporting atrocities.<sup id="cite_ref-dk_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dk-44">[43]</a></sup> The Soviet military facilitated a ceasefire as ordered by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> in January 1991. In March and April 1991, Soviet interior troops were reported actively disarming militias on both sides, and deterring the inter-ethnic violence. Zviad Gamsakhurdia asserted that the Soviet leadership was encouraging South Ossetian separatism in order to force Georgia not to leave the Soviet Union. Georgia declared its independence in April 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-princeton_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-40">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result of the war, about 100,000 ethnic Ossetians fled the territory and Georgia proper, most across the border into North Ossetia. A further 23,000 ethnic Georgians fled South Ossetia to other parts of Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> Many South Ossetians were resettled in uninhabited areas of North Ossetia from which the <a href="/wiki/Ingush_people" title="Ingush people">Ingush</a> had been expelled by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Stalin</a> in 1944, leading to conflicts between Ossetians and Ingush over the right of residence in former Ingush territory.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>On 29 April 1991, the western part of South Ossetia was affected by an <a href="/wiki/1991_Racha_earthquake" title="1991 Racha earthquake">earthquake</a>, which killed 200 and left 300 families homeless.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In late 1991, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Civil_War#Civil_unrest" title="Georgian Civil War">dissent</a> was mounting against Gamsakhurdia in Georgia due to his intolerance of critics and attempts to concentrate political power.<sup id="cite_ref-princeton_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton-45">[44]</a></sup> On 22 December 1991, after a <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Georgian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1991–92 Georgian coup d'état">coup d'état</a>, Gamsakhurdia and his supporters were besieged by the opposition, which was backed by the national guard, in several government buildings in <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>. The ensuing heavy fighting resulted in over 200 casualties and left the center of the Georgian capital in ruins. On 6 January, Gamsakhurdia and several of his supporters fled the city for exile. Afterwards, the <a href="/wiki/Military_Council_(Georgia)" title="Military Council (Georgia)">Georgian military council</a>, an interim government, was formed by a triumvirate of <a href="/wiki/Jaba_Ioseliani" title="Jaba Ioseliani">Jaba Ioseliani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tengiz_Kitovani" title="Tengiz Kitovani">Tengiz Kitovani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tengiz_Sigua" title="Tengiz Sigua">Tengiz Sigua</a>, and, in March 1992, they invited <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Shevardnadze" title="Eduard Shevardnadze">Eduard Shevardnadze</a>, a former Soviet minister, to come to Georgia to assume control of the Georgian State Council.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-40">[39]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag needs to be fact-checked with the cited source(s). (November 2015)">verification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1993_Georgia_war2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1993_Georgia_war2.svg/250px-1993_Georgia_war2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1993_Georgia_war2.svg/375px-1993_Georgia_war2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1993_Georgia_war2.svg/500px-1993_Georgia_war2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1940" data-file-height="1370"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1993_Georgia_war2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Georgian_Civil_War" title="Georgian Civil War">Georgian Civil War</a> in October–December 1993
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 24 June 1992, Shevardnadze and the South Ossetian government signed the <a href="/wiki/Sochi_agreement" title="Sochi agreement">Sochi ceasefire agreement</a>, brokered by Russia. The agreement included obligations to avoid the use of force, and Georgia pledged not to impose sanctions against South Ossetia. The Georgian government retained control over substantial portions of South Ossetia,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> including the town of <a href="/wiki/Akhalgori" title="Akhalgori">Akhalgori</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A <a href="/wiki/Joint_Control_Commission_for_Georgian%E2%80%93Ossetian_Conflict_Resolution" title="Joint Control Commission for Georgian–Ossetian Conflict Resolution">Joined Peacekeeping force</a> of Ossetians, Russians and Georgians was established. On 6 November 1992, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE) set up a mission in Georgia to monitor the peacekeeping operation. From then until mid-2004, South Ossetia was generally peaceful.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Following the 2003 <a href="/wiki/Rose_Revolution" title="Rose Revolution">Rose Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a> became the President of Georgia in 2004. Ahead of the 2004 parliamentary and presidential elections, he promised to restore the territorial integrity of Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> During one of his early speeches, Saakashvili addressed the separatist regions, saying, "[N]either Georgia nor its president will put up with disintegration of Georgia. Therefore, we offer immediate negotiations to our Abkhazian and Ossetian friends. We are ready to discuss every model of statehood by taking into consideration their interests for the promotion of their future development."<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2004, tensions began to rise as the Georgian authorities strengthened their efforts to bring the region back under their rule. Georgia sent police to close down a black market, which was one of the region's chief sources of revenue, selling foodstuffs and fuel smuggled from Russia. This was followed by fighting by Georgian troops and peacekeepers against South Ossetian militiamen and freelance fighters from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> Hostage takings, shootouts and occasional bombings left dozens dead and wounded. A ceasefire deal was reached on 13 August though it was repeatedly violated.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The Georgian government protested against the allegedly increasing Russian economic and political presence in the region and against the uncontrolled military of the South Ossetian side.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It also considered the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Control_Commission_for_Georgian%E2%80%93Ossetian_Conflict_Resolution" title="Joint Control Commission for Georgian–Ossetian Conflict Resolution">peacekeeping force</a> (consisting in equal parts of South Ossetians, North Ossetians, Russians and Georgians) to be non-neutral and demanded its replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2015)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Biden" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Biden">Joseph Biden</a> (Chairman, U.S. Senate Foreign Relations Committee), <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lugar" title="Richard Lugar">Richard Lugar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mel_Martinez" class="mw-redirect" title="Mel Martinez">Mel Martinez</a> sponsored a resolution accusing Russia of attempting to undermine Georgia's territorial integrity and called for replacing the Russian-manned peacekeeping force operating under CIS mandate.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> According to U.S. senator <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lugar" title="Richard Lugar">Richard Lugar</a>, the United States supported Georgia's call for the withdrawal of Russian peacekeepers from the conflict zones.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> Later, EU South Caucasus envoy Peter Semneby said that "Russia's actions in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Georgian-Russian_espionage_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 Georgian-Russian espionage controversy">Georgia spy row</a> have damaged its credibility as a neutral peacekeeper in the EU's Black Sea neighbourhood."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_war">2008 war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2008 war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War" title="Russo-Georgian War">Russo-Georgian War</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/2008_Russo-Georgian_diplomatic_crisis" title="2008 Russo-Georgian diplomatic crisis">Tensions between Georgia and Russia began escalating</a> in April 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-shelling_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shelling-56">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tall_order_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tall_order-57">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-counterproductive_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-counterproductive-58">[57]</a></sup> A bomb explosion on 1 August 2008 targeted a car transporting Georgian peacekeepers. South Ossetians were responsible for instigating this incident, which marked the opening of hostilities and injured five Georgian servicemen. In response,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> several South Ossetian militiamen were hit.<sup id="cite_ref-feud_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-feud-60">[59]</a></sup> South Ossetian separatists began shelling Georgian villages on 1 August. These artillery attacks caused Georgian servicemen to return fire periodically since 1 August.<sup id="cite_ref-shelling_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shelling-56">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-feud_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-feud-60">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Allison_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allison-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg/220px-Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg/330px-Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg/440px-Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dom_v_Tshinvali_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tskhinvali in August 2008
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At around 19:00 on 7 August 2008, Georgian president Mikheil Saakashvili announced a unilateral <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">ceasefire</a> and called for peace talks.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> However, escalating assaults against Georgian villages (located in the South Ossetian conflict zone) were soon matched with gunfire from Georgian troops,<sup id="cite_ref-Jamestown_Goals_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jamestown_Goals-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> who then proceeded to move in the direction of the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Self-proclaimed" title="Self-proclaimed">self-proclaimed</a> Republic of South Ossetia (<a href="/wiki/Tskhinvali" title="Tskhinvali">Tskhinvali</a>) on the night of 8 August, reaching its center in the morning of 8 August.<sup id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-67">[66]</a></sup> One Georgian diplomat told Russian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Kommersant" title="Kommersant">Kommersant</a></i> on 8 August that by taking control of Tskhinvali, <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a> wanted to demonstrate that Georgia would not tolerate the killing of Georgian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-rmd_source_1_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rmd_source_1-68">[67]</a></sup> According to Russian military expert <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Felgenhauer" title="Pavel Felgenhauer">Pavel Felgenhauer</a>, the Ossetian provocation was aimed at triggering the Georgian response, which was needed as a <a href="/wiki/Pretext" title="Pretext">pretext</a> for premeditated Russian military invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> According to Georgian intelligence,<sup id="cite_ref-NYTFreshev_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTFreshev-70">[69]</a></sup> and several Russian media reports, parts of the regular (non-peacekeeping) Russian Army had already moved to South Ossetian territory through the <a href="/wiki/Roki_Tunnel" title="Roki Tunnel">Roki Tunnel</a> before the Georgian military action.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russia accused Georgia of "aggression against South Ossetia",<sup id="cite_ref-roudik_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roudik-33">[32]</a></sup> and launched a large-scale land, air and sea invasion of Georgia with the pretext of "<a href="/wiki/Peace_enforcement" title="Peace enforcement">peace enforcement</a>" operation on 8 August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Allison_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allison-62">[61]</a></sup> Russian <a href="/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">airstrikes</a> against targets within Georgia were also launched.<sup id="cite_ref-radar_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radar-72">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Abkhazia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Abkhazia">Abkhaz forces</a> opened a second front on 9 August by <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Kodori_Valley" title="Battle of the Kodori Valley">attacking the Kodori Gorge</a>, held by Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> Tskhinvali was seized by the Russian military by 10 August.<sup id="cite_ref-radar_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radar-72">[71]</a></sup> Russian forces occupied the Georgian cities of <a href="/wiki/Zugdidi" title="Zugdidi">Zugdidi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-new_front_deeper_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new_front_deeper-74">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Senaki" title="Senaki">Senaki</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gori_central_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gori_central-75">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Poti" title="Poti">Poti</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Russia_NYTimes_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Russia_NYTimes-76">[75]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gori,_Georgia" title="Gori, Georgia">Gori</a> (the last one after the ceasefire agreement was negotiated).<sup id="cite_ref-gori_major_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gori_major-77">[76]</a></sup> The Russian <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_Fleet" title="Black Sea Fleet">Black Sea Fleet</a> blockaded the Georgian coast.<sup id="cite_ref-Allison_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allison-62">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A campaign of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_of_Georgians_in_South_Ossetia" title="Ethnic cleansing of Georgians in South Ossetia">ethnic cleansing against Georgians in South Ossetia</a> was conducted by South Ossetians,<sup id="cite_ref-Fact-finding_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fact-finding-78">[77]</a></sup> with Georgian villages around Tskhinvali being destroyed after the war had ended.<sup id="cite_ref-Damage_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Damage-79">[78]</a></sup> The war displaced 192,000 people,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> and while many were able to return to their homes after the war, a year later around 30,000 ethnic Georgians remained displaced.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> In an interview published in <i>Kommersant</i>, South Ossetian leader <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Kokoity" title="Eduard Kokoity">Eduard Kokoity</a> said he would not allow Georgians to return.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of France</a> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> negotiated a ceasefire agreement on 12 August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> On 17 August, Russian president <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> announced that Russian forces would begin to pull out of Georgia the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-http_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http-85">[84]</a></sup> Russia recognised Abkhazia and South Ossetia as separate republics on 26 August.<sup id="cite_ref-kremlin_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kremlin-86">[85]</a></sup> In response to Russia's recognition, the Georgian government severed diplomatic relations with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-break_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-break-87">[86]</a></sup> Russian forces left the buffer areas bordering <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> and South Ossetia on 8 October and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Monitoring_Mission" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union Monitoring Mission">European Union Monitoring Mission</a> in Georgia assumed authority over the buffer areas.<sup id="cite_ref-en.rian_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.rian-88">[87]</a></sup> Since the war, Georgia has maintained that Abkhazia and South Ossetia are <a href="/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia" title="Occupied territories of Georgia">Russian-occupied Georgian territories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-parliament.ge_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parliament.ge-89">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 30 September 2009, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>–sponsored <i>Independent International Fact-Finding Mission on the Conflict in Georgia</i> stated that, while preceded by months of mutual provocations, "open hostilities began with a large-scale Georgian military operation against the town of Tskhinvali and the surrounding areas, launched in the night of 7 to 8 August 2008."<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Geography"></span> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Georgia_(country)" title="Geography of Georgia (country)">Geography of Georgia (country)</a>
      </div>

           <a href="/wiki/File:Georgia_high_detail_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Georgia_high_detail_map.png/200px-Georgia_high_detail_map.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="148" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Georgia_high_detail_map.png/300px-Georgia_high_detail_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Georgia_high_detail_map.png/400px-Georgia_high_detail_map.png 2x" data-file-width="2529" data-file-height="1872"></a>
