         </div> 
        </div></li> 
      </ul> 
      <p>South Ossetia is in the very heart of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> at the juncture of Asia and Europe, and it occupies the southern slopes of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">Greater Caucasus</a> Mountain Range and the foothills' part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kartalin_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kartalin Valley (page does not exist)">Kartalin Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Republic_of_South_Ossetia_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Republic_of_South_Ossetia-94">[93]</a></sup> South Ossetia is a very mountainous region. The <a href="/wiki/Likhi_Range" title="Likhi Range">Likhi Range</a> is roughly in the center of South Ossetia,<sup id="cite_ref-Cac_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cac-95">[94]</a></sup> and the plateau that's also roughly in the center of South Ossetia is called <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Iberia" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasian Iberia">Iberia</a>. </p>
      <p>The Greater Caucasus Mountain Range forms the northern border of South Ossetia with Russia, and the main roads through the mountain range into Russian territory lead through the <a href="/wiki/Roki_Tunnel" title="Roki Tunnel">Roki Tunnel</a> between South and <a href="/wiki/North_Ossetia" class="mw-redirect" title="North Ossetia">North Ossetia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Darial_Gorge" title="Darial Gorge">Darial Gorge</a>. The Roki Tunnel was vital for the <a href="/wiki/Russian_military" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian military">Russian military</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia war">2008 South Ossetia war</a> because it is the only direct route through the Caucasus Mountains. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus_regions_map3.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Caucasus_regions_map3.png/220px-Caucasus_regions_map3.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Caucasus_regions_map3.png/330px-Caucasus_regions_map3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Caucasus_regions_map3.png/440px-Caucasus_regions_map3.png 2x" data-file-width="2070" data-file-height="1789"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus_regions_map3.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The breakaway republics of South Ossetia, <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a> within the Caucasus region
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Ossetia covers an area of about 3,900&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,506&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> separated by the mountains from the more populous North Ossetia (which is part of Russia) and extending southwards almost to the <a href="/wiki/Mtkvari" class="mw-redirect" title="Mtkvari">Mtkvari</a> river in Georgia. More than 89% of South Ossetia lies over 1,000&nbsp;m (3,281&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>, and its highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Khalatsa" title="Mount Khalatsa">Mount Khalatsa</a> at 3,938&nbsp;m (12,920&nbsp;ft) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-South_Ossetia_Maps_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Ossetia_Maps-97">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nearby <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kazbek" title="Mount Kazbek">Mount Kazbek</a> is 5,047&nbsp;m (16,558&nbsp;ft), and it is of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> origin. The region between Kazbek and <a href="/wiki/Shkhara" title="Shkhara">Shkhara</a> (a distance of about 200&nbsp;km (124&nbsp;mi) along the Main Caucasus Range) is dominated by numerous glaciers. Out of the 2,100 glaciers that exist in the Caucasus today, approximately <a href="/wiki/Glaciers_of_Georgia" title="Glaciers of Georgia">30% are located within Georgia</a> which South Ossetia forms a part of. </p>
      <p>The term <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Caucasus" title="Lesser Caucasus">Lesser Caucasus Mountains</a> is often used to describe the mountainous (highland) areas of southern Georgia that are connected to the Greater Caucasus Mountain Range by the <a href="/wiki/Likhi_Range" title="Likhi Range">Likhi Range</a>. The overall region can be characterized as being made up of various, interconnected mountain ranges (largely of volcanic origin) and plateaus that do not exceed 3,400 meters (11,155&nbsp;ft) in elevation. </p>
      <p>Most of South Ossetia is in the <a href="/wiki/Kura_(Caspian_Sea)" title="Kura (Caspian Sea)">Kura Basin</a> with the rest of it in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> basin. The <a href="/wiki/Likhi_Range" title="Likhi Range">Likhi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racha" title="Racha">Racha</a> ridges act as divide separating these two <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">basins</a>. Major rivers in South Ossetia include the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Liakhvi_River" title="Greater Liakhvi River">Greater</a> and Little Liakhvi, <a href="/wiki/Ksani" title="Ksani">Ksani</a>, Medzhuda, Tlidon, Canal Saltanis, Ptsa River and host of other tributaries.<sup id="cite_ref-South_Ossetia_Maps_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Ossetia_Maps-97">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>South Ossetia's climate is affected by <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical</a> influences from the East and <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a> influences from the West. The Greater Caucasus range moderates the local climate by serving as a barrier against cold air from the north, which results in the fact that, even at great heights, it is warmer there than in the Northern Caucasus.<sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Republic_of_South_Ossetia_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Republic_of_South_Ossetia-94">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-South_Ossetia_Maps_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Ossetia_Maps-97">[96]</a></sup> Climatic zones in South Ossetia are determined by distance from the Black Sea and by altitude. The plains of eastern Georgia are shielded from the influence of the Black Sea by mountains that provide a more <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a>. </p>
      <p>The foothills and mountainous areas (including the Greater Caucasus Mountains) experience cool, wet summers and snowy winters, with snow cover often exceeding two meters in many regions. The penetration of humid air masses from the Black Sea to the west of South Ossetia is often blocked by the <a href="/wiki/Likhi_Range" title="Likhi Range">Likhi</a> mountain range. The wettest periods of the year in South Ossetia generally occur during spring and autumn while the winter and summer months tend to be the driest. Elevation plays an important role in South Ossetia where climatic conditions above 1,500 metres (4,921&nbsp;ft) are considerably colder than in any lower-lying areas. The regions that lie above 2,000 metres (6,562&nbsp;ft) frequently experience frost even during the summer months. </p>
      <p>The average temperature in South Ossetia in January is around +4 degrees Celsius, and the average temperature in July is around +20.3 degrees Celsius. The average yearly liquid precipitation in South Ossetia is around 598 millimeters.<sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Republic_of_South_Ossetia_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Republic_of_South_Ossetia-94">[93]</a></sup> In general, summer temperatures average 20&nbsp;°C (68&nbsp;°F) to 24&nbsp;°C (75.2&nbsp;°F) across much of South Ossetia, and winter temperatures average 2&nbsp;°C (35.6&nbsp;°F) to 4&nbsp;°C (39.2&nbsp;°F). Humidity is relatively low and rainfall across South Ossetia averages 500 to 800&nbsp;mm (19.7 to 31.5&nbsp;in) per year. <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">Alpine</a> and highland regions have distinct <a href="/wiki/Microclimates" class="mw-redirect" title="Microclimates">microclimates</a> though. At higher elevations, precipitation is sometimes twice as heavy as in the eastern plains of Georgia. Alpine conditions begin at about 2,100&nbsp;m (6,890&nbsp;ft), and above 3,600&nbsp;m (11,811&nbsp;ft) snow and ice are present year-round. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_status">Political status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Political status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_South_Ossetia" title="Foreign relations of South Ossetia">Foreign relations of South Ossetia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png/220px-Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png/330px-Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png/440px-Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png 2x" data-file-width="2481" data-file-height="3508"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Decree_recognising_South_Ossetia_independence.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ukaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukaz">Russian Presidential Decree</a> No. 1261 recognising South Ossetian independence.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia war">2008 South Ossetia war</a>, Russia recognized South Ossetia as independent.<sup id="cite_ref-join_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-join-98">[97]</a></sup> This unilateral recognition by Russia was met by condemnation from <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> Blocs, such as <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> due to the violation of Georgia's territorial integrity.<sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-99">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-civil.ge_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civil.ge-100">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-101">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-102">[101]</a></sup> The EU's diplomatic response to the news was delayed by disagreements between eastern European states, the UK wanting a harsher response and Germany, France and other states' desire not to isolate Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> Former US envoy <a href="/wiki/Richard_Holbrooke" title="Richard Holbrooke">Richard Holbrooke</a> said the conflict could encourage separatist movements in other former Soviet states along Russia's western border.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> Several days later, Nicaragua became the second country to recognize South Ossetia.<sup id="cite_ref-join_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-join-98">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> recognized South Ossetia on 10 September 2009, becoming the third UN member state to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-Venezuela_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venezuela-105">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, North Atlantic Treaty Organization (<a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>) and most UN member countries do not recognize South Ossetia as an independent state. The <i>de facto</i> republic governed by the secessionist government held a second <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_independence_referendum,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="South Ossetian independence referendum, 2006">independence referendum</a><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-106">[105]</a></sup> on 12 November 2006, after its first referendum in 1992 was not recognized by most governments as valid.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> According to the Tskhinvali election authorities, the referendum turned out a majority for independence from Georgia where 99% of South Ossetian voters supported independence and the turnout for the vote was 95%.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> The referendum was monitored by a team of 34 international <a href="/wiki/Election_observers" class="mw-redirect" title="Election observers">observers</a> from Germany, Austria, Poland, Sweden and other countries at 78 polling stations.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> However, it was not recognized internationally by the UN, European Union, OSCE, NATO and the Russian Federation, given the lack of ethnic Georgian participation and the illegality of such a referendum without recognition from the Georgian government in <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> The European Union, OSCE and NATO condemned the referendum. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_%D0%B2_%D0%A6%D1%85%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>South Ossetia on 9 May 2018
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Parallel to the secessionist held referendum and elections, to <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Kokoity" title="Eduard Kokoity">Eduard Kokoity</a>, the then <a href="/wiki/President_of_South_Ossetia" title="President of South Ossetia">President of South Ossetia</a>, the Ossetian opposition movement (<a href="/wiki/People_of_South_Ossetia_for_Peace" title="People of South Ossetia for Peace">People of South Ossetia for Peace</a>) organized their own elections contemporaneously in Georgian-controlled areas within South Ossetia, in which Georgian and some Ossetian inhabitants of the region voted in favour of <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Sanakoyev" title="Dmitry Sanakoyev">Dmitry Sanakoyev</a> as the alternative President of South Ossetia.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-111">[110]</a></sup> The alternative elections of Sanakoyev claimed full support of the ethnic Georgian population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In April 2007, Georgia created the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Administrative_Entity_of_South_Ossetia" class="mw-redirect" title="Provisional Administrative Entity of South Ossetia">Provisional Administrative Entity of South Ossetia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> staffed by ethnic <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetian</a> members of the separatist movement. <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Sanakoyev" title="Dmitry Sanakoyev">Dmitry Sanakoyev</a> was assigned as the leader of the Entity. It was intended that this provisional administration would negotiate with central Georgian authorities regarding its final status and conflict resolution.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> On 10 May 2007, Sanakoyev was appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Georgia" title="President of Georgia">President of Georgia</a> as the Head of South Ossetian Provisional Administrative Entity. </p>
      <p>On 13 July 2007, Georgia set up a state commission, chaired by the Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Zurab_Noghaideli" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurab Noghaideli">Zurab Noghaideli</a>, to develop South Ossetia's autonomous status within the Georgian state. According to the Georgian officials, the status was to be elaborated within the framework of "an all-inclusive dialogue" with all the forces and communities within the Ossetian society.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>South Ossetia, <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Artsakh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> are sometimes referred to as post-Soviet "<a href="/wiki/Frozen_conflict" title="Frozen conflict">frozen conflict</a>" zones.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans_of_integration_with_the_Russian_Federation">Plans of integration with the Russian Federation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Plans of integration with the Russian Federation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg/260px-Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg/390px-Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg/520px-Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="778" data-file-height="749"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Military_bases_in_Tskhinvali_Region_of_Georgia.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russian military bases in South Ossetia as of 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 30 August 2008, Tarzan Kokoity, the Deputy Speaker of South Ossetia's parliament, announced that the region would soon be absorbed into Russia, so that South and North Ossetians could live together in one united Russian state.<sup id="cite_ref-times0830_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times0830-120">[119]</a></sup> Russian and South Ossetian forces began giving residents in <a href="/wiki/Akhalgori" title="Akhalgori">Akhalgori</a>, the biggest town in the predominantly ethnic Georgian eastern part of South Ossetia, the choice of accepting Russian citizenship or leaving.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Kokoity" title="Eduard Kokoity">Eduard Kokoity</a>, the then president of South Ossetia, later stated that South Ossetia would not forgo its independence by joining Russia: "We are not going to say no to our independence, which has been achieved at the expense of many lives; South Ossetia has no plans to join Russia." <a href="/wiki/Civil_Georgia" title="Civil Georgia">Civil Georgia</a> has said that this statement contradicts previous ones made by Kokoity earlier that day, when he indicated that South Ossetia would join <a href="/wiki/North_Ossetia%E2%80%93Alania" title="North Ossetia–Alania">North Ossetia</a> in the Russian Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-times0830_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times0830-120">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The South Ossetian and Russian presidents signed an "alliance and integration" treaty on 18 March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-integration_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-integration-123">[122]</a></sup> The agreement includes provisions to incorporate the South Ossetian military into Russia's armed forces, integrate the customs service of South Ossetia into that of Russia's, and commit Russia to paying state worker salaries in South Ossetia at rates equal to those in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus_Federal_District" class="mw-redirect" title="North Caucasus Federal District">North Caucasus Federal District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> described the treaty as calling for "nearly full integration" and compared it to a 2014 agreement between Russia and <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-integration_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-integration-123">[122]</a></sup> The Georgian Foreign Ministry described the signing of the treaty as "actual annexation" of the disputed region by Russia, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> said they would not recognize it.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In another move towards integration with the Russian Federation, South Ossetian President <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Tibilov" title="Leonid Tibilov">Leonid Tibilov</a> proposed in December 2015 a name change to "<b>South Ossetia–Alania</b>" – in analogy with "<a href="/wiki/North_Ossetia%E2%80%93Alania" title="North Ossetia–Alania">North Ossetia–Alania</a>", a Russian federal subject. Tibilov furthermore suggested holding a referendum on joining the Russian Federation prior to April 2017, which would lead to a united "Ossetia–Alania".<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> In April 2016, Tibilov said he intended to hold the referendum before August of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> However, on 30 May, Tibilov postponed the referendum until after the presidential election due in April 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_name_change_referendum,_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="South Ossetian name change referendum, 2017">name-change referendum</a>, nearly 80 percent of those who voted endorsed the name-change, while the presidential race was won by <a href="/wiki/Anatoliy_Bibilov" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatoliy Bibilov">Anatoliy Bibilov</a> – against the incumbent, Tibilov, who had been supported by Moscow and who, unlike Bibilov, was ready to heed Moscow's wish for the integration referendum not be held any time soon.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_on_Occupied_Territories_of_Georgia">Law on Occupied Territories of Georgia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Law on Occupied Territories of Georgia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia" title="Occupied territories of Georgia">Occupied territories of Georgia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG/220px-South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG/330px-South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG/440px-South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="534"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:South_Ossetian_landscape.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Landscape in South Ossetia's Dzhava District
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In late October 2008, President Saakashvili signed into law legislation on the occupied territories passed by the Georgian Parliament. The law covers the breakaway regions of Abkhazia and Tskhinvali (territories of former South Ossetian Autonomous Oblast).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> The law spells out restrictions on free movement and economic activity in the territories. In particular, according to the law, foreign citizens should enter the two breakaway regions only through Georgia proper. Entry into Abkhazia should be carried out from the <a href="/wiki/Zugdidi_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Zugdidi District">Zugdidi District</a> and into South Ossetia from the <a href="/wiki/Gori_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Gori District">Gori District</a>. The major road leading to South Ossetia from the rest of Georgia passes through the Gori District.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The legislation, however, also lists "special" cases in which entry into the breakaway regions will not be regarded as illegal. It stipulates that a special permit on entry into the breakaway regions can be issued if the trip there "serves Georgia's state interests; peaceful resolution of the conflict; de-occupation or humanitarian purposes." The law also bans any type of economic activity – entrepreneurial or non- entrepreneurial, if such activities require permits, licenses or registration in accordance with Georgian legislation. It also bans air, sea and railway communications and international transit via the regions, mineral exploration and money transfers. The provision covering economic activities is retroactive, going back to 1990.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The law says that the Russian Federation – the state which has carried out military occupation – is fully responsible for the violation of human rights in Abkhazia and South Ossetia. The Russian Federation, according to the document, is also responsible for compensation of material and moral damage inflicted on Georgian citizens, stateless persons and foreign citizens, who are in Georgia and enter the occupied territories with appropriate permits. The law also says that de facto state agencies and officials operating in the occupied territories are regarded by Georgia as illegal. The law will remain in force until "the full restoration of Georgian jurisdiction" over the breakaway regions is realised.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2009, during the opening ceremony of a new Georgian Embassy building in <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>, Ukraine, Georgian President <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a> stated that residents of South Ossetia and <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> could also use its facilities: "I would like to assure you, my dear friends, that this is your home, as well, and here you will always be able to find support and understanding".<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

        <tr>
         <td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style>
          <div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini">
           <ul>
            <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_South_Ossetia" title="Template:Politics of South Ossetia"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_South_Ossetia" title="Template talk:Politics of South Ossetia"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Until the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia war">armed conflict of August 2008</a>, South Ossetia consisted of a checkerboard of Georgian-inhabited and Ossetian-inhabited towns and villages.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> The largely Ossetian capital city of <a href="/wiki/Tskhinvali" title="Tskhinvali">Tskhinvali</a> and most of the other Ossetian-inhabited communities were governed by the separatist government, while the Georgian-inhabited villages and towns were administered by the Georgian government. This close proximity and the intermixing of the two communities has made the <a href="/wiki/Georgian%E2%80%93Ossetian_conflict" title="Georgian–Ossetian conflict">Georgian–Ossetian conflict</a> particularly dangerous, since any attempt to create an ethnically pure territory would involve <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer" title="Population transfer">population transfers</a> on a large scale. </p>
      <p>The political dispute has yet to be resolved and the South Ossetian separatist authorities govern the region with effective independence from Tbilisi. Although talks have been held periodically between the two sides, little progress was made under the government of <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Shevardnadze" title="Eduard Shevardnadze">Eduard Shevardnadze</a> (1993–2003). His successor <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a> (elected 2004) made the reassertion of Georgian governmental authority a political priority. Having successfully put an end to the <i>de facto</i> independence of the southwestern province of <a href="/wiki/Ajaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Ajaria">Ajaria</a> in May 2004, he pledged to seek a similar solution in South Ossetia. After the 2004 clashes, the Georgian government has intensified its efforts to bring the problem to international attention. On 25 January 2005, President Saakashvili presented a Georgian vision for resolving the South Ossetian conflict at the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Assembly_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe">Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe</a> session in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>. Late in October, the US government and the OSCE expressed their support to the Georgian action plan presented by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Zurab_Noghaideli" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurab Noghaideli">Zurab Noghaideli</a> at the OSCE Permanent Council at <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> on 27 October 2005. On 6 December, the OSCE Ministerial Council in <a href="/wiki/Ljubljana" title="Ljubljana">Ljubljana</a> adopted a resolution supporting the Georgian peace plan<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> which was subsequently rejected by the South Ossetian <i>de facto</i> authorities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Under Article 46 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_South_Ossetia" title="Constitution of South Ossetia">Constitution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_South_Ossetia" title="President of South Ossetia">president</a> of the Republic of South Ossetia is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and head of the executive branch of government. The president of RSO is elected by direct popular vote for five years. Since 21 April 2017, the position is held by <a href="/wiki/Anatoliy_Bibilov" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatoliy Bibilov">Anatoliy Bibilov</a> who won a contested <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_presidential_election,_2017" class="mw-redirect" title="South Ossetian presidential election, 2017">election</a> running against the incumbent, <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Tibilov" title="Leonid Tibilov">Leonid Tibilov</a>. </p>
      <p>The country's legislative body is the unicameral <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Ossetia" title="Parliament of South Ossetia">Parliament of South Ossetia</a> that comprises 34 members elected by popular vote for five years. </p>
      <p>The government of South Ossetia is a component of the integrated system of the executive branch. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_South_Ossetia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of South Ossetia">Military of South Ossetia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>South Ossetia's armed forces in 2017 were partially incorporated into the Armed Forces of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg/220px-Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg/330px-Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg/440px-Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="977" data-file-height="1111"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Caucasus-ethnic_en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ethnic map of the Caucasus from 1995 <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a> live in North and South Ossetia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Georgian-Ossetian_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian-Ossetian conflict">Georgian-Ossetian conflict</a> roughly two-thirds of the population of South Ossetia was <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetian</a> and 25–30% was <a href="/wiki/Georgian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgian people">Georgian</a>. The eastern quarter of the country, around the town and district of <a href="/wiki/Akhalgori" title="Akhalgori">Akhalgori</a>, was predominantly Georgian, while the center and west were predominantly Ossetian. Much of the mountainous north is sparsely inhabited. (See map at <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Caucasus" title="Languages of the Caucasus">Languages of the Caucasus</a>.) </p>
      <p>Because the statistical office of Georgia was not able to conduct the 2002 Georgian census in South Ossetia, the present composition of the population of South Ossetia is unknown,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> although according to some estimates there were 47,000 ethnic Ossetians and 17,500 ethnic Georgians in South Ossetia in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg/220px-Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg/330px-Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg/440px-Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="514"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Palm_Sunday_procession_in_Tskhinvali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Palm_Sunday" title="Palm Sunday">Palm Sunday</a> procession in Tskhinvali
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>2009 population estimate: During the war, according to Georgian officials, 15,000 Georgians moved to Georgia proper; South Ossetian officials indicate that 30,000 Ossetians fled to North Ossetia, and a total of 500 citizens of South Ossetia were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> This left the estimated population at 54,500. However, Russia's reconstruction plan involving 600 million dollars in aid to South Ossetia may have spur immigration into the area, especially with Russia's movement of 3,700 soldiers into South Ossetia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> RIA Novosti places the population of South Ossetia at 80,000, although this figure is probably too optimistic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2015 census conducted by the South Ossetian authorities, the region's total population was 53,532, including 48,146 Ossetians (89.9%), 3,966 Georgians (7.4%), and 610 Russians. Of these, 30,432 lived in Tskhinvali. The Georgian authorities have questioned the accuracy of these data.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> Estimates based on official birth rates and school attendence suggest it may have around 39,000 inhabitants, and an independent estimate from 2009 put the population at 26,000.<sup id="cite_ref-3DCFTAs_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3DCFTAs-144">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox Christianity">Eastern Orthodox Christianity</a> is the major religion practiced in South Ossetia, by Ossetians, Georgians and Russians.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg/220px-Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg/330px-Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg/440px-Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dzuarikau-Tskhinval.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Dzuarikau%E2%80%93Tskhinvali_pipeline" title="Dzuarikau–Tskhinvali pipeline">Dzuarikau–Tskhinvali pipeline</a>, delivering <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> from Russia to South Ossetia, went online in 2009.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>South Ossetia's economy is primarily agricultural, although less than 10% of South Ossetia's land area is cultivated. Cereals, fruit and vines are the major produce. Forestry and cattle industries are also maintained. A number of industrial facilities also exist, particularly around the capital, Tskhinvali. Following the war in the 1990s, South Ossetia struggled economically. South Ossetian GDP was estimated at US$15&nbsp;million (US$250 per capita) in a work published in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> Employment and supplies are scarce. Additionally, Georgia cut off supplies of electricity to the region, which forced the South Ossetian government to run an electric cable through North Ossetia. The majority of the population survives on subsistence farming. Virtually the only significant economic asset that South Ossetia possesses is control of the <a href="/wiki/Roki_Tunnel" title="Roki Tunnel">Roki Tunnel</a> that is used to link Russia and Georgia, from which the South Ossetian government reportedly obtained as much as a third of its budget by levying customs duties on freight traffic before the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Georgian_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Georgian war">war</a>. </p>
      <p>President Eduard Kokoity has admitted that his country is seriously dependent on Russian economic assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-ap_econ_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ap_econ-150">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>South Ossetia's <a href="/wiki/Poverty_threshold" title="Poverty threshold">poverty threshold</a> stood at 3,062 rubles a month in the fourth quarter of 2007, or 23.5 percent below Russia's average, while South Ossetians have incomparably smaller incomes.<sup id="cite_ref-delyagin_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delyagin-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia war">2008 South Ossetia war</a>, South Ossetia's industry consisted of 22 small factories, with a total production of 61.6&nbsp;million rubles in 2006. In 2007, only 7 factories were functioning. In March 2009, it was reported that most of the production facilities were standing idle and were in need of repairs. Even successful factories have a shortage of workers, are in debt and have a shortage of working capital.<sup id="cite_ref-delyagin_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delyagin-151">[150]</a></sup> One of the largest local enterprises is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Emalprovod&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Emalprovod (page does not exist)">Emalprovod</a> factory, which has 130 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-delyagin_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delyagin-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The South Ossetian authorities are planning to improve finances by boosting the local production of flour and thus reducing the need for flour imports. For this purpose, the area planted with wheat was increased tenfold in 2008 from 130 hectares to 1,500 hectares. The wheat harvest in 2008 was expected to be 2,500 tons of grain. The South Ossetian Agriculture ministry also imported some tractors in 2008, and was expecting delivery of more farm machinery in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-delyagin_151-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delyagin-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russia planned to spend 10&nbsp;billion rubles in the restoration of South Ossetia in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-delyagin_151-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delyagin-151">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The economy is currently very dependent on funding from Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy_Army_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy_Army-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, the Administration of South Ossetia estimated its GDP to be nearly 0.1&nbsp;billion US dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-investrso.su_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investrso.su-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_music" title="Ossetian music">Ossetian music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Women_in_South_Ossetia" title="Women in South Ossetia">Women in South Ossetia</a>
      </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The country's principal university is <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetian_State_University" title="South Ossetian State University">South Ossetian State University</a> in Tskhinvali.<sup id="cite_ref-uwn_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uwn-153">[152]</a></sup> After the Russo-Georgian War in 2008, education officials attempted to place most university-bound students from South Ossetia in Russian <a href="/wiki/Post-secondary_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-secondary education">post-secondary education</a> institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-uwn_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uwn-153">[152]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_Holidays">Public Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Ossetia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Public Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_South_Ossetia" title="Public holidays in South Ossetia">Public holidays in South Ossetia</a>
      </div>
